# Leader Election Patterns Across K8s Ecosystem

## Your Task

Compare leader election implementations across kubernetes/kubernetes and etcd-io/etcd. Find Go source files in each repo that implement leader election: the lease-based election in k8s, the Raft-based leader in etcd, and how each handles leader failover and re-election.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

    17→// Package leaderelection implements leader election of a set of endpoints.
    18→// It uses an annotation in the endpoints object to store the record of the
    19→// election state. This implementation does not guarantee that only one
    20→// client is acting as a leader (a.k.a. fencing).
    21→//
    22→// A client only acts on timestamps captured locally to infer the state of the
    23→// leader election. The client does not consider timestamps in the leader
    24→// election record to be accurate because these timestamps may not have been
    25→// produced by a local clock. The implemention does not depend on their
    26→// accuracy and only uses their change to indicate that another client has
    27→// renewed the leader lease. Thus the implementation is tolerant to arbitrary
    28→// clock skew, but is not tolerant to arbitrary clock skew rate.
    29→//
    30→// However the level of tolerance to skew rate can be configured by setting
    31→// RenewDeadline and LeaseDuration appropriately. The tolerance expressed as a
    32→// maximum tolerated ratio of time passed on the f
... (truncated)

    32→type leader struct {
    33→	ctx context.Context
    34→	w   clientv3.Watcher
    35→	// mu protects leaderc updates.
    36→	mu       sync.RWMutex
    37→	leaderc  chan struct{}
    38→	disconnc chan struct{}
    39→	donec    chan struct{}
    40→}
    41→
    42→func newLeader(ctx context.Context, w clientv3.Watcher) *leader {
    43→	l := &leader{
    44→		ctx:      clientv3.WithRequireLeader(ctx),
    45→		w:        w,
    46→		leaderc:  make(chan struct{}),
    47→		disconnc: make(chan struct{}),
    48→		donec:    make(chan struct{}),
    49→	}
    50→	// begin assuming leader is lost
    51→	close(l.leaderc)
    52→	go l.recvLoop()
    53→	return l
    54→}
    55→

    57→	defer close(l.donec)

  1238→func (s *EtcdServer) isLeader() bool {

  1242→// MoveLeader transfers the leader to the given transferee.
  1243→func (s *EtcdServer) MoveLeader(ctx context.Context, lead, transferee uint64) error {
  1244→	member := s.cluster.Member(types.ID(transferee))
  1245→	if member == nil || member.IsLearner {
  1246→		return errors.ErrBadLeaderTransferee
  1247→	}
  1248→
  1249→	now := time.Now()
  1250→	interval := time.Duration(s.Cfg.TickMs) * time.Millisecond
  1251→
  1252→	lg := s.Logger()
  1253→	lg.Info(
  1254→		"leadership transfer starting",
  1255→		zap.String("local-member-id", s.MemberID().String()),
  1256→		zap.String("current-leader-member-id", types.ID(lead).String()),
  1257→		zap.String("transferee-member-id", types.ID(transferee).String()),
  1258→	)
  1259→
  1260→	s.r.TransferLeadership(ctx, lead, transferee)
  1261→	for s.Lead() != transferee {
  1262→		select {
  1263→		case <-ctx.Done(): // time out
  1264→			return errors.ErrTimeoutLeaderTransfer
  1265→		case <-time.After(interval):
  1266→		}
  1267→	}
  1268→
  1269→	// TODO: drain all requests, or drop all messages to the old leader
  1270→	lg.Info(
  1271→		"leadership transfer finished",
  1272→		zap.String("local-member-id", s.MemberID().String()),
  1273→		zap.String("old-leader-member-id", types.ID(lead).String()),
  1274→		zap.String("new-leader-member-id", types.ID(transferee).String()),
  1275→		zap.Duration("took", time.Since(now)),
  1276→	)
  1277→	return nil
  1278→}

   914→// ensureLeadership checks whether current member is still the leader.
   915→func (s *EtcdServer) ensureLeadership() bool {
   916→	lg := s.Logger()
   917→
   918→	if s.isActive() {
   919→		lg.Debug("The member is active, skip checking leadership",
   920→			zap.Time("latestTickTs", s.r.getLatestTickTs()),
   921→			zap.Time("now", time.Now()))
   922→		return true
   923→	}
   924→
   925→	ctx, cancel := context.WithTimeout(s.ctx, s.Cfg.ReqTimeout())
   926→	defer cancel()
   927→	if err := s.linearizableReadNotify(ctx); err != nil {
   928→		lg.Warn("Failed to check current member's leadership",
   929→			zap.Error(err))
   930→		return false
   931→	}
   932→

   937→			zap.Uint64("new-lead", newLeaderID))
   938→		return false
   939→	}
   940→
   941→	return true
   942→}

// HardStop stops the server without coordination with other members in the cluster.
func (s *EtcdServer) HardStop() {
	select {
	case s.stop <- struct{}{}:
	case <-s.done:
		return
	}
	<-s.done
}

   109→// Proclaim lets the leader announce a new value without another election.
   110→func (e *Election) Proclaim(ctx context.Context, val string) error {
   111→	if e.leaderSession == nil {
   112→		return ErrElectionNotLeader
   113→	}
   114→	client := e.session.Client()
   115→	cmp := v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(e.leaderKey), "=", e.leaderRev)
   116→	txn := client.Txn(ctx).If(cmp)
   117→	txn = txn.Then(v3.OpPut(e.leaderKey, val, v3.WithLease(e.leaderSession.Lease())))
   118→	tresp, terr := txn.Commit()
   119→	if terr != nil {
   120→		return terr
   121→	}
   122→	if !tresp.Succeeded {
   123→		e.leaderKey = ""
   124→		return ErrElectionNotLeader
   125→	}
   126→
   127→	e.hdr = tresp.Header
   128→	return nil
   129→}
   130→
   131→// Resign lets a leader start a new election.
   132→func (e *Election) Resign(ctx context.Context) (err error) {
   133→	if e.leaderSession == nil {
   134→		return nil
   135→	}
   136→	client := e.session.Client()
   137→	cmp := v3.Compare(v3.CreateRevision(e.leaderKey), "=", e.leaderRev)
   138→	resp, err := client.Txn(ctx).If(cmp).Then(v3.OpDelete(e.leaderKey)).Commit()
   139→	if err == nil {
   140→		e.hdr = resp.Header
   141→	}
   142→	e.leaderKey = ""
   143→	e.leaderSession = nil
   144→	return err
   145→}
   146→

   153→	} else if len(resp.Kvs) == 0 {
   154→		// no l

## Leader Election, Leases, and Leader Failover in Kubernetes

I've found a comprehensive set of files related to leader election, lease management, and leader failover in the Kubernetes codebase. Here are the most relevant files and their key functions/types:

### Core Leader Election Implementation

#### 1. **Main Leader Election Client**
**File:** `/workspace/kubernetes/staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`

**Key Types & Functions:**
- `LeaderElector` - Main struct for leader election
- `LeaderElectionConfig` - Configuration for leader election with `LeaseDuration`, `RenewDeadline`, `RetryPeriod`
- `LeaderCallbacks` - Callbacks structure with:
  - `OnStartedLeading()` - Called when candidate becomes leader
  - `OnStoppedLeading()` - Called when candidate stops leading
  - `OnNewLeader()` - Called when a new leader is observed
- `NewLeaderElector()` - Creates a LeaderElector
- `Run()` - Main run loop that coordinates acquire/renew cycles
- `acquire()` - Attempts to acquire leadership lease
- `renew()` - Renews the leadership lease periodically
- `tryAcquireOrRenew()` - Core fast/slow path lease acquisition/renewal logic
- `tryCoordinatedRenew()` - Coordinated leader election mode with preferred holders
- `release()` - Releases the lease on shutdown
- `IsLeader()` - Checks if this instance is the current leader
- `GetLeader()` - Returns identity of current leader
- `Check()` - Health check for lease validity

**Lease Timing Configuration:**
- Default `LeaseDuration`: 15 seconds
- Default `RenewDeadline`: 10 seconds  
- Default `RetryPeriod`: 2 seconds

153-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully analyzed leader election patterns across both the Kubernetes and etcd ecosystems and created the comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Summary of Findings

**Kubernetes Implementation (Lease-Based):**
- Core files: `leaderelection.go`, `leaselock.go`, and coordinated election controllers
- Uses distributed Lease objects as locks with explicit timing (15s lease duration, 10s renewal deadline)
- Includes coordinated election mode that prefers older/stable nodes
- Failover occurs when lease expires; non-leaders detect expiry and compete to acquire
- Graceful transitions via `PreferredHolder` field and `LeaseCandidate` objects

**etcd Implementation (Raft-Based):**
- Core files: `raft.go`, `server.go`, and transport layer
- Uses Raft consensus algorithm for automatic leader election via quorum
- Faster failover via election timeouts (typically 150-300ms vs Kubernetes's 15s)
- Graceful leadership transfer via `MoveLeader()` using `longestConnected()` strategy
- Client-side election API in `election.go` for application-level leader elections

**Key Differences:**
1. Kubernetes relies on explicit distributed leases; etcd on Raft consensus
2. Kubernetes failover takes ~15s; etcd typically ~150-300ms
3. Kubernetes prefers old nodes for stability; etcd prefers longest-connected
4. Kubernetes is control-plane focused; etcd exposes election as a client API

The answer file includes 21 relevant files, 31 key symbols, and an execution chain showing how both systems implement leader election and failover.

Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a distributed lease mechanism that operates independently of the control plane's etcd backend consensus. The core implementation is in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, which provides the `LeaderElector` type that manages the acquisition and renewal of leases.\\n\\n**Core Mechanism:**\\nThe `LeaderElector` type in `leaderelection.go` implements a client-side leader election protocol with configurable timing: a default lease duration of 15 seconds, renewal deadline of 10 seconds, and retry period of 2 seconds. The main `Run()` function orchestrates a continuous loop that attempts to acquire or renew leadership using the `tryAcquireOrRenew()` function. Leadership is stored in Kubernetes `Lease` objects, which act as distributed locks.\\n\\n**Lease-Based Lock Implementation:**\\nThe `LeaseLock` type in `resourcelock/leaselock.go` implements the `Interface` defined in `resourcelock/interface.go`. It stores election metadata in the Lease resource's spec field, including `HolderIdentity` (current leader), `LeaseDurationSeconds`, `AcquireTime`, `RenewTime`, and `LeaderTransitions` count. The `LeaderElectionRecord` structure encapsulates these fields.\\n\\n**Failover and Re-election:**\\nWhen the current leader fails to renew its lease within the `RenewDeadline` (10 seconds), the lease expires after the `LeaseDuration` (15 seconds). Non-leader instances detect this expiry and attempt acquisition. The `isLeaseExpired()` function in `election.go` checks if the current time exceeds `RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds`. Upon failover, any remaining candidate can acquire the lease and become leader.\\n\\n**Coordinated Election Mode:**\\nKubernetes also implements an optional coordinated election strategy using `LeaseCandidate` objects in `leasecandidate.go`. The `Controller` in `leaderelection_controller.go` runs the `reconcileElectionStep()` function, which periodically (every 5 seconds) sends ping times to registered candidates and collects their acknowledgments. The controller then invokes `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` from `election.go` to select the best candidate based on emulation version (backward compatibility) and binary version. This graceful approach prefers older, more stable nodes for leadership, with a 30-minute validity window for candidates enforced by the `LeaseCandidateGCController` in `leasecandidategc_controller.go`.\\n\\n**API Server Peer Discovery:**\\nThe `PeerEndpointLeaseController` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/reconcilers/peer_endpoint_lease.go` uses a similar lease mechanism to register API server endpoints, enabling peer discovery during version skew scenarios.\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for leader election, where leadership is determined by Raft's quorum-based election mechanism rather than distributed locks. The core Raft implementation is in `server/etcdserver/raft.go`.\\n\\n**Raft Leader Detection:**\\nThe `raftNode` type in `raft.go` wraps the Raft state machine. The `start()` function processes Raft ready states, monitoring `SoftState.Lead` to detect leadership changes. When `rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None`, a new leader has been elected, triggering calls to the `updateLeadership` callback. This detection is automatic and quorum-based\u2014no explicit leases are required.\\n\\n**Server-Side Leadership Management:**\\nThe `EtcdServer` type in `server/etcdserver/server.go` provides leadership query functions: `Lead()` returns the current leader ID as a uint64, `Leader()` returns it as a `types.ID`, and `isLeader()` checks if the local node is the leader. The `setLead()` and `getLead()` functions atomically manage the leader ID. The `ensureLeadership()` function performs a linearizable read to verify the current member still holds leadership.\\n\\n**Automatic Failover:**\\nWhen a leader fails, the Raft algorithm automatically triggers an election timeout. Remaining members detect the leader's absence and initiate an election where a new leader is chosen by Raft consensus. The `advanceTicks()` function in `raft.go` adjusts election timing for multi-datacenter deployments, preventing unnecessary frequent elections during network latency.\\n\\n**Graceful Leadership Transfer:**\\nThe `MoveLeader()` function in `server.go` explicitly transfers leadership to a specified node. It validates the transferee is not a learner and calls `s.r.TransferLeadership()` from the underlying Raft library. The transfer polls `s.Lead()` until the transfer completes or times out. The `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` function gracefully transfers leadership on shutdown, using `longestConnected()` from `util.go` to identify the most reliable candidate\u2014the member with the oldest \\\"active-since\\\" connection time.\\n\\n**Member Health Tracking:**\\nThe `Transporter` interface in `api/rafthttp/transport.go` provides `ActiveSince(id types.ID)` to return when a peer was last successfully contacted. The `longestConnected()` utility uses this to find members with stable, long-lived connections, making them preferred leadership transfer targets.\\n\\n**Failover Testing:**\\nEnd-to-end and integration tests in `tests/e2e/failover_test.go` and `tests/integration/v3_failover_test.go` validate failover behavior during defragmentation, server shutdowns, and cluster operations.\\n\\n**Client-Side Election:**\\nFor application-level leader election, etcd provides the `Election` type in `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`. Applications call `Campaign()` to enter the election, `Resign()` to step down, and `Observe()` to watch for leader changes. This is separate from the server's Raft-based leadership and is built on top of etcd's key-value storage and leasing mechanisms.\\n\\n**Leadership Transfer CLI:**\\nThe `move_leader_command.go` in etcdctl provides the `move-leader` command, allowing operators to manually trigger leadership transfers. It finds the current leader via Status RPC and validates the target member before calling the client's `MoveLeader()` RPC.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Consensus Mechanism:** Kubernetes uses explicit lease-based election independent of its backing store; etcd uses Raft's built-in consensus for server leadership.\\n2. **Timing:** Kubernetes leases have explicit duration timers (15s lease, 10s renewal deadline); Raft uses election timeouts (customizable via configuration).\\n3. **Failover Speed:** Kubernetes requires lease expiry time (up to 15s); Raft typically elects a new leader within one election timeout (typically 150-300ms).\\n4. **Transfer Strategy:** Kubernetes coordinated mode prefers stable (older version) nodes; etcd prefers the longest-connected node.\\n5. **Graceful Shutdown:** Kubernetes controls its own graceful transitions via `PreferredHolder`; etcd uses Raft's `TransferLeadership()` mechanism.\\n6. **Client API:** Kubernetes leader election is internal to control plane components; etcd exposes client-side election through the gRPC election service in `api/v3election/election.go`.\"\n}\n",

{\"repo\": \"etcd-io/etcd\", \"path\": \"client/v3/concurrency/election.go\", \"symbol\": \"Resign\"}\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"## Leader Election Patterns: Kubernetes vs etcd\\n\\n### Kubernetes: Lease-Based Leader Election\\n\\nKubernetes implements leader election through a distributed lease mechanism that operates independently of the control plane's etcd backend consensus. The core implementation is in `staging/src/k8s.io/client-go/tools/leaderelection/leaderelection.go`, which provides the `LeaderElector` type that manages the acquisition and renewal of leases.\\n\\n**Core Mechanism:**\\nThe `LeaderElector` type in `leaderelection.go` implements a client-side leader election protocol with configurable timing: a default lease duration of 15 seconds, renewal deadline of 10 seconds, and retry period of 2 seconds. The main `Run()` function orchestrates a continuous loop that attempts to acquire or renew leadership using the `tryAcquireOrRenew()` function. Leadership is stored in Kubernetes `Lease` objects, which act as distributed locks.\\n\\n**Lease-Based Lock Implementation:**\\nThe `LeaseLock` type in `resourcelock/leaselock.go` implements the `Interface` defined in `resourcelock/interface.go`. It stores election metadata in the Lease resource's spec field, including `HolderIdentity` (current leader), `LeaseDurationSeconds`, `AcquireTime`, `RenewTime`, and `LeaderTransitions` count. The `LeaderElectionRecord` structure encapsulates these fields.\\n\\n**Failover and Re-election:**\\nWhen the current leader fails to renew its lease within the `RenewDeadline` (10 seconds), the lease expires after the `LeaseDuration` (15 seconds). Non-leader instances detect this expiry and attempt acquisition. The `isLeaseExpired()` function in `election.go` checks if the current time exceeds `RenewTime + LeaseDurationSeconds`. Upon failover, any remaining candidate can acquire the lease and become leader.\\n\\n**Coordinated Election Mode:**\\nKubernetes also implements an optional coordinated election strategy using `LeaseCandidate` objects in `leasecandidate.go`. The `Controller` in `leaderelection_controller.go` runs the `reconcileElectionStep()` function, which periodically (every 5 seconds) sends ping times to registered candidates and collects their acknowledgments. The controller then invokes `pickBestLeaderOldestEmulationVersion()` from `election.go` to select the best candidate based on emulation version (backward compatibility) and binary version. This graceful approach prefers older, more stable nodes for leadership, with a 30-minute validity window for candidates enforced by the `LeaseCandidateGCController` in `leasecandidategc_controller.go`.\\n\\n**API Server Peer Discovery:**\\nThe `PeerEndpointLeaseController` in `staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/reconcilers/peer_endpoint_lease.go` uses a similar lease mechanism to register API server endpoints, enabling peer discovery during version skew scenarios.\\n\\n### etcd: Raft-Based Leader Election\\n\\netcd uses the Raft consensus algorithm for leader election, where leadership is determined by Raft's quorum-based election mechanism rather than distributed locks. The core Raft implementation is in `server/etcdserver/raft.go`.\\n\\n**Raft Leader Detection:**\\nThe `raftNode` type in `raft.go` wraps the Raft state machine. The `start()` function processes Raft ready states, monitoring `SoftState.Lead` to detect leadership changes. When `rd.SoftState.Lead != raft.None`, a new leader has been elected, triggering calls to the `updateLeadership` callback. This detection is automatic and quorum-based\u2014no explicit leases are required.\\n\\n**Server-Side Leadership Management:**\\nThe `EtcdServer` type in `server/etcdserver/server.go` provides leadership query functions: `Lead()` returns the current leader ID as a uint64, `Leader()` returns it as a `types.ID`, and `isLeader()` checks if the local node is the leader. The `setLead()` and `getLead()` functions atomically manage the leader ID. The `ensureLeadership()` function performs a linearizable read to verify the current member still holds leadership.\\n\\n**Automatic Failover:**\\nWhen a leader fails, the Raft algorithm automatically triggers an election timeout. Remaining members detect the leader's absence and initiate an election where a new leader is chosen by Raft consensus. The `advanceTicks()` function in `raft.go` adjusts election timing for multi-datacenter deployments, preventing unnecessary frequent elections during network latency.\\n\\n**Graceful Leadership Transfer:**\\nThe `MoveLeader()` function in `server.go` explicitly transfers leadership to a specified node. It validates the transferee is not a learner and calls `s.r.TransferLeadership()` from the underlying Raft library. The transfer polls `s.Lead()` until the transfer completes or times out. The `TryTransferLeadershipOnShutdown()` function gracefully transfers leadership on shutdown, using `longestConnected()` from `util.go` to identify the most reliable candidate\u2014the member with the oldest \\\"active-since\\\" connection time.\\n\\n**Member Health Tracking:**\\nThe `Transporter` interface in `api/rafthttp/transport.go` provides `ActiveSince(id types.ID)` to return when a peer was last successfully contacted. The `longestConnected()` utility uses this to find members with stable, long-lived connections, making them preferred leadership transfer targets.\\n\\n**Failover Testing:**\\nEnd-to-end and integration tests in `tests/e2e/failover_test.go` and `tests/integration/v3_failover_test.go` validate failover behavior during defragmentation, server shutdowns, and cluster operations.\\n\\n**Client-Side Election:**\\nFor application-level leader election, etcd provides the `Election` type in `client/v3/concurrency/election.go`. Applications call `Campaign()` to enter the election, `Resign()` to step down, and `Observe()` to watch for leader changes. This is separate from the server's Raft-based leadership and is built on top of etcd's key-value storage and leasing mechanisms.\\n\\n**Leadership Transfer CLI:**\\nThe `move_leader_command.go` in etcdctl provides the `move-leader` command, allowing operators to manually trigger leadership transfers. It finds the current leader via Status RPC and validates the target member before calling the client's `MoveLeader()` RPC.\\n\\n### Key Differences\\n\\n1. **Consensus Mechanism:** Kubernetes uses explicit lease-based election independent of its backing store; etcd uses Raft's built-in consensus for server leadership.\\n2. **Timing:** Kubernetes leases have explicit duration timers (15s lease, 10s renewal deadline); Raft uses election timeouts (customizable via configuration).\\n3. **Failover Speed:** Kubernetes requires lease expiry time (up to 15s); Raft typically elects a new leader within one election timeout (typically 150-300ms).\\n4. **Transfer Strategy:** Kubernetes coordinated mode prefers stable (older version) nodes; etcd prefers the longest-connected node.\\n5. **Graceful Shutdown:** Kubernetes controls its own graceful transitions via `PreferredHolder`; etcd uses Raft's `TransferLeadership()` mechanism.\\n6. **Client API:** Kubernetes leader election is internal to control plane components; etcd exposes client-side election through the gRPC election service in `api/v3election/election.go`.\"\n}\n",
